TITLE      Neutron inelastic cross-section measurements for 24Mg  23258  1    3 
REFERENCE  (J,PR/C,90,034603,2014)                                23258  1    4 
           #doi:10.1103/PhysRevC.90.034603                        23258  1    5 
           (S,AIP-1852,080006,2017) same data, new analysis       23258  1    6 
AUTHOR     (A.Olacel,C.Borcea,P.Dessagne,M.Kerveno,A.Negret,      23258  1    7 
           A.J.M.Plompen)                                         23258  1    8 
INSTITUTE  (2ZZZGEL) A.J.M.Plompen.                               23258  1    9 
           (3RUMBUC) A.Olacel,C.Borcea,A.Negret.                  23258  1   10 
           (3RUMBUU) A.Olacel.                                    23258  1   11 
           (2FR STR) P.Dessagne,M.Kerveno.                        23258  1   12 
FACILITY   (LINAC,2ZZZGEL) ToF facility GELINA.                   23258  1   13 
           Station located 200 m from the neutron source.         23258  1   14 
           GAINS (Gamma Array for Inelastic Neutron Scattering)   23258  1   15 
           setup.                                                 23258  1   16 
INC-SOURCE (PHOTO) Electrons accelerated to 70-140 MeV with a     23258  1   17 
           repetition rate of 800 Hz and a FWHM of the pulse <1ns 23258  1   18 
           bremsstrahlung in a rotating depleted uranium target.  23258  1   19 
           The neutrons are produced through U(g,xn) and U(g,f)   23258  1   20 
           reactions. Neutron beam was collimated to a diameter of23258  1   21 
           61 mm and the energy-integrated flux was ~ 500 n/cm2/s.23258  1   22 
           Two filters were used:                                 23258  1   23 
           - 10B (1.23 g/cm2)                                     23258  1   24 
           - natU (36.8 g/cm2),                                   23258  1   25 
           both placed in the middle of the source-sample distance23258  1   26 
           to avoid moderated neutrons and to attenuate the gamma 23258  1   27 
           flash proceeding the neutron pulses.                   23258  1   28 
METHOD     (TOF)                                                  23258  1   29 
           Neutron energy resolution of ~1 keV at 1MeV and up to  23258  1   30 
           ~ 35 keV at 10MeV .                                    23258  1   31 
           The differential gamma production cross section at     23258  1   32 
           angles of 150. and 110. deg in the energy range from   23258  1   33 
           threshold energy up to 18 MeV were measured.           23258  1   34 
           The angle integrated gamma production cross sections   23258  1   35 
           were determined in the same energy range.              23258  1   36 
           The total inelastic cross section and the level cross  23258  1   37 
           sections were calculated using the low excitation      23258  1   38 
           energy level scheme of 24Mg from the evaluated         23258  1   39 
           database.                                              23258  1   40 
DETECTOR   (HPGE) GAINS consisted of 8 large-volume high-purity Ge23258  1   41 
           detectors (only 7 of them were active ) placed at 110  23258  1   42 
           and 150 deg with respect to the beam direction, with   23258  1   43 
           four detectors at each angle, at distances of 14-16.5cm23258  1   44 
           from the target.                                       23258  1   45 
           Gamma energy resolution - 2.3 keV for the 1332 keV peak23258  1   46 
           of 60Co and 100% relative efficiency.                  23258  1   47 
           The calibration measurements were taken with a         23258  1   48 
           point-like 152Eu source ( activity 18.9 +- 0.6 kBq).   23258  1   49 
           The determination of the setup efficiency was performed23258  1   50 
           by a method combining calibration measurements and     23258  1   51 
           MCNP5 simulations.                                     23258  1   52 
           (FISCH) The neutron flux was monitored with a 235U     23258  1   53 
           fission chamber placed in the measurement station.     23258  1   54 
           For the threshold used in this measurement the         23258  1   55 
           efficiency of the fission chamber was 84+-2 %.         23258  1   56 
SAMPLE     24Mg sample of diameter of 8.003 +- 0.001 cm, area     23258  1   57 
           density of 0.698 +- 0.001 g/cm2, was irradiated at a   23258  1   58 
           distance of 19868.4 cm from the neutron source.        23258  1   59 
MONITOR    (92-U-235(N,F),,SIG)                                   23258  1   60 
ANALYSIS   Examined gammas:                                       23258  1   61 
           Egamma Eini  JPI-ini Efin  JPIfin Igamma Multipolarity 23258  1   62

CORRECTION -For multiple scattering.                              23258  1   79

           Above the neutron energy of 7.6MeV, the total inelastic23258  1   81

ERR-ANALYS (ERR-S) The statistical uncertainties of the detector  23258  1   89 
           yields ~ 2%.                                           23258  1   90 
           (ERR-1) Uncertainty due to HPGe efficiency calibration 23258  1   91 
            (mainly from the activity of the source and the       23258  1   92 
            positioning of the calibration source) - 2% .         23258  1   93 
           (ERR-2,,1.) The uncertainty of the multiple scattering 23258  1   94 
           correction factor calculated from the MCNP5 simulations23258  1   95 
           < 1% .                                                 23258  1   96 
           (MONIT-ERR) Uncertainty of 235U(n,F) cross section from23258  1   97

           (ERR-3) Uncertainty of the fission chamber efficiency  23258  1   99 
           - 2%.                                                  23258  1  100 
           (ERR-T)     The total resulting uncertainty for the    23258  1  101 
           strongest transitions is of the order of 5% .          23258  1  102
